Sunnah vs Fard in Wudu: Hanafi-Maliki Dispute
Dispute on whether sunnah acts of wudu are obligatory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies the sunnah acts of wudu as sunnah muakkadah and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument using the criteria of thubut and dalala.

Core Idea
The Prophet's consistent practice (muwazabah) indicates sunnah, not fard, unless a qat'i proof establishes obligation.

This lesson examines the dispute between the Hanafi and Maliki schools regarding the legal status of the sunnah acts of wudu. While both schools acknowledge the Prophet's continuous practice, they differ on whether that practice establishes obligation. The Hanafi school maintains that these acts are emphatic sunnah, relying on the principle that ahad hadith cannot establish fard. By understanding this dispute, you will learn how the Hanafi school evaluates evidence and resolves conflicts between apparent commands and foundational usul principles.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi and Maliki positions
Identify the exact claim: Hanafi says the acts are sunnah muakkadah; Maliki says they are fard. Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).
2
Analyze the Maliki dalil
The hadith of Umar commanding repetition for a missed spot. Determine its thubut (ahad) and the apparent dalala (imperative).
Maliki takes the imperative as indicating obligation.
3
Apply the Hanafi response
The hadith is ahad and cannot establish fard (qat'i). The command can be interpreted as emphasis on sunnah. Also, the narration from Ibn Umar contradicts Maliki's claim about continuity being fard.
Hanafi usul: ahad hadith is zanni al-thubut and cannot override the silence of Quran and mutawatir.
4
Examine the muwazabah principle
The Prophet's continuous practice (muwazabah) indicates sunnah unless there is independent qat'i evidence of obligation. The commentator clarifies that 'without evidence' means no valid evidence exists in this case.
Continuous practice of obligatory acts (like prayer) is also present, but those have separate qat'i proof.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice: Hanafi deems wudu valid if these acts are omitted (but deficient); Maliki deems it invalid. This affects daily worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعند مالك ه : هو فرض ، والدليل على كون الأمور المذكورة سنة مواظبة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من غير دليل على فرضيتها". أن عمر رضى الله عنه رأى رجلاً توضأ فبقي في رجله قدر ظفر فقال: أعد الوضوء، ونحوه في «مسند الإمام أحمد». وبهذا استند مالك لله في افتراض الولاء ، وليس بصحيح، فإنّ هذه أخبار آحاد لا تثبت الافتراض مع كون القرآن والأحاديث المشهورة ساكتة عنه ، على أن الأمر بالإعادة يستقيم على تقدير السنية أيضاً، اهتماماً بشأن السنن. وقد أخرج مالك له في «الموطأ» : «إنّ ابن عمر له توضأ فغسل وجهه ويديه ومسح برأسه، ثم دعي بجنازة ليصلي عليها حين دخل المسجد، فمسح على خفيه وهذا نص على عدم كون الولاء فرضاً. [١]قوله : من غير دليل على فرضيّتها ؛ إنّما زاد هذا لئلا يرد أنه قد واظب على الفرائض كالصلاة والصوم فيلزم أن تكون سنة، والمراد بالافتراض ما يشمل الوجوب أيضا. فحاصله : أنَّ المواظبة إنّما تدلّ على السنيّة إذا لم يدلّ دليل آخر على كون ذلك الأمر الذي واظب عليه فرضاً أو واجباً، وهذه الأمور المذكورة كذلك، والمراد بالمواظبة المداومة مع الترك أحياناً كما سيصرح به في تعريف السنة. فإن قلت : قد مرَّ أنَّ بعض الأئمة ذهبوا إلى افتراض بعض الأشياء المذكورة، وأقاموا عليه الأدلة، فلا يصح قوله : «من غير دليل على فرضيتها». قلت : لما كانت الدلائل المذكورة مقدوحة عندنا جعل وجودها كالعدم.
According to Malik, it (i.e., these acts) is obligatory. The evidence that the mentioned acts are sunnah is the Prophet's continuous practice without evidence of their being obligatory. That Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) saw a man performing wudu, and there remained on his foot the size of a fingernail, so he said: 'Repeat the wudu,' and similar is in Musnad Ahmad. And on this Malik based his view of the obligation of continuity, but it is not correct, because these are ahad reports that do not establish obligation, especially since the Qur'an and well-known ahadith are silent about it. Moreover, the command to repeat is also consistent with the interpretation of sunnah, out of emphasis for sunnah. And Malik also narrated in al-Muwatta': 'Ibn Umar performed wudu, washing his face and hands and wiping his head, then was called for a funeral prayer when he entered the mosque, so he wiped over his leather socks, and this is clear evidence that continuity is not obligatory.' [Commentary] His statement: 'without evidence of their being obligatory'; he added this only lest it be objected that he continuously performed obligatory acts like prayer and fasting, so it would follow that they are sunnah. And what is meant by obligation includes wajib. So the gist: continuous practice indicates sunnah only if no other evidence indicates that the performed act is fard or wajib. And these mentioned acts are such. And what is meant by continuous practice is persistence with occasional omission, as will be clarified in the definition of sunnah. If you say: Some imams have held some of the mentioned acts to be obligatory and have presented evidence, so his statement 'without evidence of their being obligatory' is not correct. I say: Since those evidences are contested by us, their existence is considered nonexistent.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Maliki schools concerning the legal status of certain acts in wudu—such as rinsing the mouth and sniffing water. The Hanafi position is that these acts are sunnah, not obligatory (fard). The author first states the Maliki view that they are fard. The evidence for the Hanafi view is the Prophet's consistent practice (muwazabah) without any proof of obligation. The passage then critiques the Maliki reliance on the hadith in which Umar ordered a man to repeat his wudu for leaving a nail-sized spot dry. The author argues that this is an ahad report, which cannot establish obligation, especially since the Qur'an and widely known hadith are silent. Moreover, the command to repeat can be interpreted as emphasis on the sunnah, not as indicating obligation. Additionally, a narration from Ibn Umar in al-Muwatta' shows that he wiped over his socks after partial wudu, proving that continuity (al-wala') is not obligatory. The commentary then explains the phrase 'without evidence of their being obligatory' to preempt the objection that the Prophet also continuously performed obligatory acts like prayer and fasting. The point is that continuous practice (muwazabah) indicates sunnah only when no other evidence establishes obligation. Since the evidence presented by other schools is considered weak (maqduh) in the Hanafi view, it is effectively nonexistent. This passage illustrates the Hanafi usul principle that ahad hadith cannot establish fard, and that consistent practice alone is not sufficient for obligation.

Key Terms
مواظبة (muwazabah): Continuous practice with occasional omission, as in the Prophet's habit.
فرض (fard): A legally obligatory act whose omission incurs sin and invalidates the act if omitted intentionally.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed but is not obligatory; omission is not sinful but is disapproved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school reject the Maliki claim that the acts of wudu (e.g., rinsing mouth) are obligatory (fard)?
A) Because these acts are not mentioned in the Quran or hadith.
B) Because the hadith used by Malik is ahad and cannot establish fard, and the command to repeat can be interpreted as emphasis of sunnah.
C) Because the Prophet never performed these acts consistently.
D) Because Malik's evidence is based on qiyas, which is not valid in wudu.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the Prophet's continuous practice (muwazabah) with occasional omission indicates sunnah, not fard, unless there is independent qat'i evidence of obligation.

Tiyamin: Starting with the Right in Wudu – Mustahabb Not Sunnah Mu'akkadah
Ruling with proof and refutation of objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on tiyamin (starting with the right in wudu), explain the evidence, and distinguish between mustahabb and sunnah mu'akkadah.

Core Idea
Starting with the right in wudu is recommended (mustahabb) but not an emphatic sunnah, because the Prophet's consistent practice may be natural rather than prescribed.

This lesson examines the ruling of starting with the right limb (tiyamin) when performing wudu. The Hanafi school holds it to be mustahabb (recommended), not sunnah mu'akkadah (emphatic sunnah). We will analyze the evidence, the definition of mustahabb, and the rebuttal to the objection that the Prophet's continuous practice should elevate it to sunnah mu'akkadah.

Guided Path
1
Define mustahabb and sunnah mu'akkadah
Understand the difference: mustahabb is recommended without sin for leaving, sunnah mu'akkadah entails sin if left.
In Hanafi terminology, mustahabb is synonymous with sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
2
Identify the evidence for tiyamin
The hadith: 'When you perform wudu, begin with your right.' Notice the imperative form.
Reported by Abu Dawud, Ibn Khuzaymah, Ibn Majah, Ibn Hibban.
3
Determine the scope of tiyamin
Which limbs are included? Only those with distinct right and left, like hands and feet. For ears, face, etc., simultaneity is recommended.
Tiyamin is not sunnah for wiping ears, washing cheeks, etc.
4
Analyze the objection
An objector says that since the Prophet consistently started with the right and never with the left, tiyamin should be sunnah mu'akkadah.
The objection relies on the principle that continuous practice (muwazabah) indicates sunnah.
5
Refute the objection
The Hanafi response: Consistency does not necessarily imply worship; it could be natural habit. Hence tiyamin remains mustahabb.
The proof for mustahabb is that the Prophet's practice may not have been intended as prescribed worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : لا شك أن [١] قوله : ومستحبه؛ هو ما يكون مطلوباً شرعاً من غير ذمّ على تركه مطلقاً بخلاف السنة المؤكدة، فإن تاركها مستحق للإثم ، ويُسمّى المستحب مندوباً وأدباً فضيلة ونفلاً أيضاً، وقد يفسر بما فعله النبي مرة وترك أخرى ولم يواظب عليه، وهذا أخص من الأول. [٢]قوله : التيامن؛ لقوله : «إذا توضأتم فابدؤوا بأيمانكم»، أخرجه أبو داود وابن خزيمة وابن ماجه ، وابن حبان . [٣]قوله : في غسل الأعضاء ؛ المراد بالغسل أعم من الغسل ومن المسح لكونه غسلاً حكميّاً ؛ فإنه يستحب التيامنُ في غسل اليدين والرجلين أيضاً، والمراد بالأعضاء الظاهرة من كل وجه، والتي لها يمين ويسار متمايز. فلا يسن التيامن في مسح الأذنين، ولا في غسل الخدين ولا في مسح الرأس والخفّين وغسل الوجه والفم والأنف، بل يستحب فيها المعية، صرح به في «السراج الوهاج» و«الجوهرة النيرة»، و«حَلْبة المجلي»، وغيرها. [٤] قوله : فإن قلت : حاصله : أنَّ الحكم باستحباب التيامن غير صحيح ؛ لأنَّ النبي واظب على التيامن ؛ إذ لم يرو أحد ممن حكى الوضوء النبوي أنه تركه وبدأ بالشمال، وكل ما هو كذلك فهو سنة. وبهذا يظهر أنّ قوله : «لا شك. .... الخ صغرى لكبرى محذوفة، دل عليه ما مرّ من أن المواظبة دليل السنيّة، وقوله : ولم يرو» دليل على الصغرى ، فلو أورد كلمة «إذ» التعليلية كان أولى، وقوله: «فينبغي» نتيجة لدليل.
If you say: There is no doubt that [1] His statement: 'its mustahabb' refers to what is legally sought without any blame for leaving it absolutely, unlike the emphatic sunnah, whose abandoner is deserving of sin. It is also called mandub, adab, fadilah, and nafl. It is also interpreted as what the Prophet did once and left another time and did not continuously practice it, and this is more specific than the first. [2] His statement: 'tiyamin' is based on his saying: 'When you perform wudu, begin with your right (organs),' reported by Abu Dawud, Ibn Khuzaymah, Ibn Majah, and Ibn Hibban. [3] His statement: 'in washing the limbs' means washing in the general sense, including wiping as a legal washing. So tiyamin is recommended in washing the hands and feet as well. The intended limbs are those that are manifest from every side and have a distinct right and left. So tiyamin is not sunnah for wiping the ears, nor for washing the cheeks, nor for wiping the head and the leather socks, nor for washing the face, mouth, and nose. Rather, simultaneity is recommended in them, as stated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, Halbat al-Mujalli, and others. [4] His statement: 'If you say' – its gist: The ruling of recommending tiyamin is incorrect because the Prophet continuously practiced it; no one who narrated the prophetic wudu reported that he left it and began with the left, and everything like that is sunnah. From this it becomes clear that his statement 'there is no doubt' is the minor premise, and the major premise is omitted, indicated by what has passed that continuous practice is evidence of sunnah. His statement 'and it is not reported' is evidence for the minor premise. So it would have been better if he used the explanatory particle 'idh'. His statement 'therefore it should be' is the result of the evidence.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on starting with the right side in wudu (tiyamin), declaring it mustahabb (recommended). The commentary begins by defining mustahabb: it is an act sought by the Law but without blame for leaving it, as opposed to the sunnah mu'akkadah (emphatic sunnah) which entails sin if left. Mustahabb is also called mandub, adab, fadilah, or nafl. It is further defined as what the Prophet sometimes did and sometimes left, without continuous adherence – a more specific definition than the general one. The evidence for tiyamin is the hadith: 'When you perform wudu, begin with your right (organs).' This is reported by several hadith masters. The commentary then specifies which limbs are included: only limbs that are manifest and have a distinct left and right, such as hands and feet. For actions like wiping the ears, washing the cheeks, wiping the head, socks, face, mouth, and nose, tiyamin is not sunnah; rather, one should wash them together (simultaneity). Finally, an objection is raised: since the Prophet consistently practiced tiyamin and no one reported him starting with the left, why is it not sunnah? The commentary refutes this by noting that the definition of sunnah requires continuous practice done as an act of worship. The Prophet's consistent practice of tiyamin could be due to his natural inclination, not necessarily as prescribed worship. Therefore, it remains mustahabb, not sunnah. The logical structure is that the objection is the minor premise, the major premise (muwazabah indicates sunnah) is implied, and the conclusion that it should be sunnah is rejected because the minor premise is incomplete – the Prophet's continuous practice alone does not make it sunnah without the intention of worship.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): A legally sought action whose omission is not blameworthy, as opposed to sunnah muakkadah which incurs sin if abandoned.
التيامن (al-tiyamin): The act of starting with the right side or right limb in wudu.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah muakkadah): An emphatic sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed and whose abandoner is sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is starting with the right (tiyamin) in wudu considered mustahabb and not sunnah muakkadah in the Hanafi school?
A) Because the hadith commanding it is weak.
B) Because the Prophet did not always start with the right; he sometimes started with the left.
C) Because the Prophet's consistent practice may be due to his natural habit, not necessarily as an act of worship, and no one reported him starting with the left.
D) Because the Hanafi school does not accept the hadith.

Key Takeaway
Tiyamin (starting with the right) in wudu is mustahabb in the Hanafi school because the Prophet's consistent practice may be natural rather than worshipful; thus it is recommended, not obligatory to the level of sunnah mu'akkadah.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Starting with the Right in Wudu
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the rank of al-tayamun

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding al-tayamun and apply the Hanafi definition of sunnah to distinguish between mustahabb and sunnah.

Core Idea
Starting with the right in wudu is sunnah, not just mustahabb, because of the Prophet's persistent practice.

In this lesson, we explore a subtle intra-Hanafi difference: is it mustahabb or sunnah to start with the right when washing the limbs in wudu? The matn of al-Wiqayah labels it mustahabb, but the commentator argues it should be sunnah based on the Prophet's consistency. We will examine the definition of sunnah and how it applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its scope
Understand what al-tayamun means (starting with the right) and which limbs it applies to (hands and feet, not ears, face, etc.).
The passage specifies that tayamun is only for limbs with distinct right and left.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
The matn says mustahabb; the commentator and al-Qari say sunnah. Know who held each view.
Sadr al-Shari'ah and al-Halabi held mustahabb; al-Qari preferred sunnah.
3
Examine the evidence
The hadith 'When you perform wudu, begin with your right' plus the fact that the Prophet never started with the left.
The Companion's unanimous narration supports that it was his habit.
4
Apply the definition of sunnah
Sunnah is what the Prophet persisted in with occasional omission. Does the Prophet's practice meet this? Since he never omitted it, persistence is established.
The definition of sunnah fi'liyyah is persistence with occasional omission.
5
Compare the practical difference
If sunnah, it is more emphasized and leaving it is disliked; if mustahabb, it is simply recommended.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية
النبي واظب على التّيامن في غسل الأعضاء، ولم يرو أحد أنه بدأ بالشمال ، فينبغي أن يكون سنة.

[٢] قوله : السنة ما واظب ... الخ ؛ هذا هو التعريف المشهور بين الجمهور، وفيه خدشات بسطناها في «تحفة الأخيار في إحياء سنة سيّد الأبرار، ويندفع بعضها بأن يقال : هذا التعريف للسنة الفعلية لا مطلقاً، فلا يقدحُ خروج السنة الثابتة بالقول النبوي أو التقرير النبوي ، وإن المراد بما واظب ما ليس بفرض ولا واجب لا عليه ولا على أمته ، فلا ينتقض بالفرائض والواجبات العامة والخاصة.
وفائدة تقييد الترك أحياناً : أن المواظبة بلا ترك دليل الوجوب عند الجمهور والأحسنُ ما اختاره صاحب «البحر» وغيره أنّ المواظبة مطلقاً دليل السنية ما لم تقترن بالزجر على تارك ذلك الفعل بخصوصه، وإن اقترنت دلّت على الوجوب(٢)، وليطلب تحقيق هذا البحث من «التحفة»(۳).
(۱) (تحفة الأخيار» (ص۸۳).
(۲) قال ابن نجيم في البحر الرائق (۱) : ۱۷ - ۱۸: «والذي ظهر للعبد الضعيف أن السنة ما واظب عليه النبي ا ا ا ا ا ل ، لكن إن كانت لا مع الترك فهي دليل السنة المؤكدة، وإن كانت مع الترك أحياناً فهي دليل غير المؤكدة، وإن اقترنت بالإنكار على من لم يفعله فهي دلـيـل الوجوب، فافهم هذا فإن به يحصل التوفيق».. قال في النهر : وينبغي أن يقيد هذا بما إذا لم يكن ذلك المواظب عليه مما اختص وجوبه ه ه ه ه و و و و و أما إذا كان كصلاة الضحى فإن عدم الإنكار ا على من لم يفعل لا يصح أن ينزل منزلة الترك، ولا بد أن يقيد الترك بكونه لغير عذر كما في التحرير ؛ ليخرج المتروك لعذر كالقيام المفروض وكأنه إنما تركه لأن الترك لعذر لا يعد تركاً».
ينظر: رد المحتار» (۱ : ۱۰۳).
(۳) (تحفة الأخيار» (ص٦٨) وما بعدها.
Book of Purity: Wudu. And its mustahabb: al-tayamun (starting with the right). (And its mustahabb: al-tayamun) meaning beginning with the right in washing the limbs. If you say: There is no doubt that his saying 'and its mustahabb' refers to what is legally desirable without blame for leaving it absolutely, unlike the emphatic sunnah, for the one who leaves it deserves sin. The mustahabb is also called mandub, adab, fadilah, and nafl. It is also defined as what the Prophet did once and left another time and did not persist in—this is more specific than the first. His saying 'al-tayamun'; because of his saying: 'When you perform wudu, begin with your right (limbs).' Narrated by Abu Dawud, Ibn Khuzaymah, Ibn Majah, and Ibn Hibban. His saying 'in washing the limbs': the intended meaning of washing is more general than washing and wiping, since it is a virtual washing. For it is mustahabb to start with the right in washing the hands and feet as well. The intended meaning of 'limbs' is those that are outwardly apparent from every side and have a distinct right and left. Thus, starting with the right is not sunnah in wiping the ears, nor in washing the cheeks, nor in wiping the head and khuffs, nor in washing the face, mouth, and nose. Rather, it is mustahabb to do them all together, as explicitly stated in 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj', 'al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah', 'Halbat al-Mujalli', and others. His saying 'If you say'—its summary: The ruling that al-tayamun is mustahabb is incorrect because the Prophet persisted in al-tayamun, for no one among those who narrated the prophetic wudu reported that he left it and began with the left, and everything that is like that is sunnah. By this it becomes clear that his saying 'there is no doubt...' is the minor premise for a suppressed major premise, which is indicated by what preceded that persistence is evidence of being sunnah. His saying 'and no one narrated' is evidence for the minor premise. So if he had used the word 'idh' (since) as a causal particle, it would have been better. His saying 'thus it should be' is the result of the evidence. (Footnote 1: Sadr al-Shari'ah in al-Nuqayah considered it mustahabb; al-Halabi in al-Multaqa did so; al-Qari in Fath Bab al-'Inayah said: 'The more correct view is that it is sunnah.' Footnote 2: From Sahih Ibn Hibban, Sunan Ibn Majah, al-Mu'jam al-Awsat, and Mawari al-Zam'an.) The Prophet persisted in al-tayamun in washing the limbs, and no one narrated that he began with the left, thus it should be sunnah. I say: The sunnah is what the Prophet persisted in with occasional omission. His saying 'and no one narrated'—it was objected that the lack of narration by anyone does not prove the actual occurrence. The response is that the Companions used to narrate all of his actions in wudu, and when they all narrated al-tayamun and no one narrated contrary to it, that indicates that al-tayamun was his habit. His saying 'the sunnah is what he persisted in...'—this is the well-known definition among the majority, and there are criticisms that we elaborated in 'Tuhfat al-Akhyar fi Ihya' Sunnat Sayyid al-Abrar'. Some of them are refuted by saying: This definition is for the actual sunnah (al-sunnah al-fi'liyyah), not absolutely, so it does not invalidate the exclusion of the sunnah established by prophetic statement or tacit approval. And what is meant by 'persisted in' is that which is not fard or wajib upon him or his ummah, so it is not invalidated by general or specific obligatory acts. The benefit of restricting 'with occasional omission' is that persistence without omission indicates obligation according to the majority. The best view is what the author of 'al-Bahr' and others chose: that persistence absolutely indicates sunnahness as long as it is not accompanied by a warning specifically for leaving that act. If it is accompanied by a warning, it indicates obligation. And let the investigation of this research be sought from 'al-Tuhfah'.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling of التيامن (starting with the right limbs) in wudu. The matn states that it is mustahabb, but the sharh raises an objection: since the Prophet always started with the right and never with the left, this should be sunnah, not mustahabb. The commentator then defines sunnah as what the Prophet persisted in with occasional omission. The objection is answered by noting that the Companions' unanimous reporting of التيامن indicates it was his habit, which supports it being sunnah. The passage then delves into a deeper discussion on the definition of sunnah, distinguishing between mustahabb and sunnah, and clarifies that the definition of sunnah as 'persistence with occasional omission' is for actual actions (sunnah fi'liyyah). The commentator also references other works that weigh the opinion that التيامن is sunnah rather than mustahabb. The practical thamarah is that if it is sunnah, there is merit in doing it and it is better to do it, but if mustahabb, it is simply recommended without the extra emphasis. The relied-upon position according to al-Qari is that it is sunnah. The passage also notes that التيامن is only recommended for limbs with distinct right and left, not for the ears, cheeks, head, or face.

Key Terms
التيامن (al-tayāmun): Beginning with the right side when washing the limbs in wudu.
مستحب (mustaḥabb): An act that is legally desirable but not obligatory; leaving it is not blameworthy.
سنة (sunnah): An act that the Prophet persisted in with occasional omission; leaving it without excuse is disliked but not sinful.
مواظبة (muwāẓabah): The Prophet's continuous practice of an act without habitual omission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the more correct view cited in the passage, what is the ruling of al-tayamun in wudu?
A) It is wajib
B) It is mustahabb
C) It is sunnah
D) It is mubah

Key Takeaway
The more correct Hanafi position is that al-tayamun in wudu is sunnah, based on the Prophet's persistent practice as reported by the Companions.

Taharah — Purification
advanced
8 min
Tayammun in Wudu: Mustahabb, Not Sunnah Mu'akkadah
Commentary on the definition of sunnah and classification of tayammun as sunan al-zawa'id

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on beginning with the right (tayammun) in wudu and explain why it is classified as sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah rather than sunnah mu'akkadah, based on the distinction between worship and habit.

Core Idea
The Prophet's continuous practice does not automatically make it sunnah mu'akkadah; intent (worship vs. habit) determines the classification.

In this passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, the commentator addresses a classic debate: does the Prophet's consistent practice of beginning with the right (tayammun) in wudu make it an emphasized sunnah? The majority of scholars define sunnah as any continuous practice with occasional omission. The Hanafi school refines this by distinguishing between acts done as worship (sunan al-huda) and acts done as habit (sunan al-zawa'id). This lesson unpacks that distinction and shows why tayammun is mustahabb, not mu'akkadah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim and objection
The matn claims tayammun is sunnah because the Prophet consistently began with the right and no one narrated otherwise. The commentator addresses an objection that lack of narration does not prove existence.
Consider the epistemological principle: absence of evidence is not evidence of absence.
2
Trace the response from the Companions
The commentator argues that because the Companions related all details of the Prophet's wudu and all agreed on tayammun, it indicates it was his habit.
This is a form of tacit agreement (ijma suktuti) among the Companions.
3
Analyze the definition of sunnah
The majority definition (continuous practice with occasional omission) is presented and critiqued. Note the refinement: it applies to active sunnah only, and consistent practice without omission does not necessarily indicate obligation; it indicates sunnah unless coupled with a specific reproach.
Ibn Nujaym's view from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is preferred: consistent practice absolutely indicates sunnah unless accompanied by reproach.
4
Distinguish sunan al-huda from sunan al-zawa'id
The crucial Hanafi distinction: if the Prophet did something as worship, it is sunnah mu'akkadah (blamed for omission); if as habit, it is sunnah zawa'id (rewarded but not blamed). The criterion is intent, not the presence or absence of omission.
Omission is not necessary for classification; the nature of the act (worship vs. custom) is decisive.
5
Apply to tayammun
The Prophet's consistency on tayammun was habitual, not devotional, as understood from his hadith 'God loves tayammun' and his practice in all matters. Therefore it is mustahabb, not mu'akkad.
The hadith uses mahabbah (love), which in Hanafi usul implies istihbab (recommendation), not obligation.

Source Text

النبي واظب على التّيامن في غسل الأعضاء، ولم يرو أحد أنه بدأ بالشمال، فينبغي أن يكون سنة.
قلتُ: السنة ما واظب عليه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مع الترك أحياناً،
[١] قوله: ولم يرو أحد؛ قد ورد عليه بأن عدم رواية أحد لا يدلّ على ثمة في نفس الأمر.
وجوابه: إن الصحابة كانوا يحكون من الوضوء النبوي جميع أفعاله، فلما حكوا بأجمعهم التيامن ولم يرو أحد خلافه دلّ ذلك على أن التيامن كان من عاداته.
[٢] قوله: السنة ما واظب... الخ؛ هذا هو التعريف المشهور بين الجمهور، وفيه خدشات بسطناها في «تحفة الأخيار في إحياء سنة سيد الأبرار»، ويندفع بعضها بأن يقال: هذا التعريف للسنة الفعلية لا مطلقاً، فلا يقدح خروج السنة الثابتة بالقول النبوي أو التقرير النبوي، وإن المراد بما واظب ما ليس بفرض ولا واجب لا عليه ولا على أمته، فلا ينتقض بالفرائض والواجبات العامة والخاصة.

(۱) (تحفة الأخيار» (ص۸۳).
(۲) قال ابن نجيم في البحر الرائق (۱): ۱۷-۱۸: «والذي ظهر للعبد الضعيف أن السنة ما واظب عليه النبي [؟]، لكن إن كانت لا مع الترك فهي دليل السنة المؤكدة، وإن كانت مع الترك أحياناً فهي دليل غير المؤكدة، وإن اقترنت بالإنكار على من لم يفعله فهي دليل الوجوب، فافهم هذا فإن به يحصل التوفيق».. قال في النهر: وينبغي أن يقيد هذا بما إذا لم يكن ذلك المواظب عليه مما اختص وجوبه [؟]، وأما إذا كان كصلاة الضحى فإن عدم الإنكار على من لم يفعل لا يصح أن ينزل منزلة الترك، ولا بد أن يقيد الترك بكونه لغير عذر كما في التحرير؛ ليخرج المتروك لعذر كالقيام المفروض وكأنه إنما تركه لأن الترك لعذر لا يعد تركاً».

كتاب الطهارة الوضوء
فإن كانت المواظبة المذكورة على سبيل العبادة فسنن الهدى، وإن كانت على سبيل العادة فسنن الزوائد كلبس النياب، والأكل باليمين، وتقديم الرجل اليمنى في الدخول، ونحو ذلك.
وكلامنا في الأول، ومواظبة النبي على التيامن كانت من قبيل الثاني، ويفهم هذا من تعليل صاحب «الهداية».
[١] قوله: فإن كانت... الخ؛ حاصل الجواب: إن ما واظب عليه الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم على قسمين:
أحدهما: سنة الهدى، ويقال لها: السنة المؤكدة، وهي التي يلام تاركها، وهي إنما تكون بالمواظبة على وجه العبادة.
وثانيهما: السنة الزائدة، وهي التي واظب عليها على سبيل العادة، وهي تساوي الاستحباب في أنه يثاب عليها ولا يلام تاركها، والمواظبة على التيامن من القسم الثاني، فلا يكون سنة مؤكدة، بل مستحباً.
[٢] قوله: وإن كانت؛ أي المواظبة المذكورة، وفيه: أنه يقتضي أن يكون الترك أحياناً معتبراً في سنن الزوائد، فيلزم أن يخرج التيامن عنها؛ إذ لم يثبت تركه كما مرّ، والتحقيق أن الترك ليس بضروري لا في سنن الهدى ولا في سنن الزوائد، وإنما الفرق بينهما بالعبادة والعادة.
(٣) قوله: ويفهم هذا؛ وجه الفهم أن تعليله بالحديث المذكور يدل على أن التيامن كان عادة له في كل شيء حتى التنعل - أي لبس النعل - والترجل - أي تسريح الشعر بالمشط - كذا ذكره ملا عصام.
وفيه ما فيه، فإن الحديث المذكور لا يدل على ما ذكره، والأوجه أن يقال: عنوان أن الله يحب يدل على أنه لو لم يكن مأموراً من الله بالتيامن على سبيل العبادة، بل لما كان التيامن محبوباً عنده تعالى، وكانت عادته اختيار ما أحبه الله داوم عليه.
The Prophet consistently began with the right in washing the limbs, and no one narrated that he started with the left, so it should be sunnah. I say: Sunnah is what the Prophet consistently practiced with occasional omission. [1] His statement: 'No one narrated' – it was objected that the lack of narration does not prove existence in reality. The response: The Companions used to relate all actions of the Prophetic ablution, and when they all related beginning with the right and no one narrated contrary, that indicates that beginning with the right was his habit. [2] His statement: 'Sunnah is what... etc.' – this is the well-known definition among the majority, and there are some criticisms which we have elaborated in 'Tuhfat al-Akhyar fi Ihya' Sunnat Sayyid al-Abrar'. Some of them are rebutted by saying: This definition applies to the active sunnah, not absolutely, so it does not invalidate sunnah established by prophetic statement or tacit approval. And what is meant by 'consistent practice' is that which is neither obligatory (fard) nor necessary (wajib) upon him or his nation, so it is not undermined by general and specific obligations. The benefit of qualifying with 'occasional omission' is that consistent practice without omission indicates obligation according to the majority. The better view is what the author of 'al-Bahr' and others chose: that consistent practice absolutely indicates sunnah status unless accompanied by reproach for the abandoner of that specific act; if accompanied by reproach, it indicates obligation (2). Let this research be sought from 'al-Tuhfah' (3). (1) (Tuhfat al-Akhyar, p. 83). (2) Ibn Nujaym said in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (1:17-18): 'What appears to the weak slave is that sunnah is what the Prophet consistently practiced [؟], but if it is without omission, it is evidence of emphasized sunnah; if with occasional omission, it is evidence of non-emphasized; if accompanied by disapproval of the one who does not do it, it is evidence of obligation. Understand this, for therein lies reconciliation.' He said in al-Nahr: 'This should be restricted to when that consistent practice is not something whose obligation is specific [؟]; but if it is like the Duha prayer, then the lack of disapproval of one who does not do it cannot be taken as omission. And omission must be without excuse, as in al-Tahrir, to exclude omission due to excuse like the obligatory standing, as if he omitted it because omission due to excuse is not considered omission.' See: Radd al-Muhtar (1:103). (3) (Tuhfat al-Akhyar, p. 68 ff.). The Book of Purification – Ablution. If the aforementioned consistent practice is in the way of worship, it is sunan al-huda; if it is in the way of habit, it is sunan al-zawa'id, like wearing clothes, eating with the right hand, entering with the right foot, etc. Our discussion is about the first, and the Prophet's consistency on beginning with the right was of the second type. This is understood from the reasoning of the author of 'al-Hidayah'. [1] His statement: 'If it was... etc.' – the gist of the answer: What the Messenger practiced is of two types: One: sunnat al-huda, called emphasized sunnah, whose abandoner is blamed, and it is only by consistent practice in the way of worship. Two: the additional sunnah, which he practiced habitually, and it equals mustahabb in that one is rewarded for it and not blamed for abandoning it. Consistency on beginning with the right is of the second type, so it is not emphasized sunnah but mustahabb. [2] His statement: 'And if it was' i.e. the aforementioned consistency. In it is that it implies that occasional omission is considered in sunan al-zawa'id, so it would require that beginning with the right be excluded from them since its omission has not been established as previously mentioned. But the reality is that omission is not necessary whether in sunan al-huda or sunan al-zawa'id; the difference between them is only by worship and habit. (3) His statement: 'And this is understood' – the understanding is that his reasoning by the mentioned hadith indicates that beginning with the right was his habit in everything, even putting on sandals – i.e., wearing the shoe – and combing – i.e., arranging the hair with a comb. So mentioned by Mulla Isam. But there is something in it, for the mentioned hadith does not indicate what he said. The more appropriate is to say: The phrase 'God loves' indicates that if he was not commanded by God to begin with the right in the way of worship, rather because beginning with the right is beloved to Him, and his habit was to choose what God loves, he persisted in it.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is a commentary on a statement from the matn (likely from al-Hidayah) that the Prophet consistently began with the right in wudu, and since no one narrated otherwise, it should be considered sunnah. The commentator first clarifies that the definition of sunnah among the majority (جمهور) is continuous practice with occasional omission. He addresses an objection that lack of narration does not prove actuality, responding that because the Companions reported all details of the Prophet's wudu and all agreed on tayammun, this indicates it was his habit. He then refines the definition: it applies only to active sunnah (sunnah fi'liyyah), not to verbal or tacit sunnah. He notes that consistent practice without omission indicates obligation according to the majority, but the preferred view from Ibn Nujaym in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is that consistent practice simply indicates sunnah unless coupled with a specific rebuke, in which case it indicates obligation. The commentator then introduces a crucial distinction: the Prophet's consistent practices are of two types: (1) Sunan al-huda (emphasized sunnah), done as worship; (2) Sunan al-zawa'id (additional sunnah), done habitually. Tayammun (beginning with the right) belongs to the second type because the Prophet did it as a habit (like wearing clothes or eating with the right hand), not as an act of worship. Therefore, it is mustahabb (recommended) and not sunnah mu'akkadah. The commentator further clarifies that occasional omission is not a necessary condition for sunan al-zawa'id; the real distinction is intent (worship vs. habit). He criticizes Mulla Isam's interpretation that the hadith 'God loves tayammun' proves habit in everything, stating instead that the hadith shows tayammun is beloved to God, and the Prophet's habit was to choose what God loves, hence he persisted in it.

Key Terms
التيامن (al-tayammun): The act of beginning with the right side or limb in actions, here specifically in washing the limbs during wudu.
السنة المؤكدة (al-sunnah al-mu'akkadah): An emphasized sunnah that the Prophet continuously performed as an act of worship, and whose abandoner is blameworthy.
سنن الزوائد (sunan al-zawa'id): Habitual or customary acts of the Prophet not done as acts of worship; one is rewarded for doing them but not blamed for omitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, the defining criterion for classifying a prophetic practice as sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized) is:
A) Consistent practice without omission
B) The presence of a command from the Prophet
C) The practice being done as an act of worship
D) The practice being reported by many Companions

Key Takeaway
Tayammun in wudu is mustahabb (sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah) because the Prophet's consistency was habitual, not devotional; the Hanafi distinction between worship and habit resolves the debate.

Taharah — Purification

Classification of Sunnah: Sunnan al-Huda and Sunnan al-Zawa'id
Explaining the basis of the Prophet's practice and its classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Sunnah al-Huda and Sunnah al-Zawa'id based on the Prophet's intention, and apply this classification to determine the ruling of tayammun.

Core Idea
The category of a sunnah depends on whether the Prophet acted out of worship or habit—not on frequency or abandonment.

In this passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, the author clarifies a crucial distinction in Hanafi fiqh: not every consistent practice of the Prophet is an emphasized sunnah. Some are habitual actions that fall under 'additional sunnah' (sunnah al-zawa'id), which are merely recommended (mustahabb). Understanding this helps us correctly classify acts like using the right hand first.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
From the passage, list the two types of consistent practices (mawazibah) of the Prophet: Sunnah al-Huda (emphasized sunnah) and Sunnah al-Zawa'id (additional sunnah).
Sunnah al-Huda is also called sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Determine the criterion for distinction
The author states that the difference is 'by worship and habit' (بالعبادة والعادة). Analyze what this means: if the Prophet acted with the intention of worship, it is Sunnah al-Huda; if habitual, it is Sunnah al-Zawa'id.
Frequency or occasional abandonment is not the criterion.
3
Apply to the case of tayammun
Using the criterion, classify the Prophet's consistent use of the right side (tayammun). The passage cites the hadith 'Allah loves tayammun' and argues that this shows it was habitual, not commanded as worship. Therefore, it is Sunnah al-Zawa'id, i.e., mustahabb.
Tayammun is recommended, not emphasized sunnah.
4
Analyze the hadith evidence
Examine the dalil: 'Allah loves tayammun in everything.' The word 'loves' indicates something beloved but not commanded, hence it is mustahabb. This is the wajh al-dalalah (indication) in Hanafi usul.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but the reasoning is sound.
5
Address the objection about occasional abandonment
The passage considers an objection that Sunnah al-Zawa'id require occasional abandonment, and since tayammun was never abandoned, it should be Sunnah al-Huda. The author refutes this, saying abandonment is not a defining feature.
The verified view (tahqiq) is that the distinction is purely by intention.

[1] قوله : فإن كانت ... الخ ؛ حاصل الجواب : إنّ ما واظب عليه الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم على قسمين : أحدهما : سنة الهدى، ويقال لها : السنة المؤكّدة، وهي التي يلام تاركها، وهي إنما تكون بالمواظبة على وجه العبادة. وثانيهما: السنة الزائدة ، وهي التي واظب عليها على سبيل العادة، وهـي تساوي الاستحباب في أنه يثاب عليها ولا يلام تاركها، والمواظبة على التيامن من القسم الثاني، فلا يكون سنة مؤكدة، بل مستحباً. [2] قوله : وإن كانت ؛ أي المواظبة المذكورة، وفيه: أنه يقتضي أن يكون التركُ أحياناً معتبراً في سنن الزوائد، فيلزم أن يخرج التيامن عنها ؛ إذ لم يثبت تركه كما مرّ، والتحقيق أن الترك ليس بضروري لا في سنن الهدى ولا في سنن الزوائد، وإنما الفرقُ بينهما بالعبادة والعادة. (٣) قوله : ويفهم هذا ؛ وجه الفهم أن تعليله بالحديث المذكور يدل على أن التيامن كان عادة له في كلّ شيء حتى التنعّل - أي لبس النعل - والترجل - أي تسريحُ الشعر بالمشط - كذا ذكره ملا عصام. وفيه ما فيه، فإنّ الحديث المذكور لا يدلّ على ما ذكره، والأوجه أن يقال : عنوان أن الله يحب يدل على أنه لو لم يكن مأموراً من الله بالتيامن على سبيل العبادة ، بل لما كان التيامن محبوباً عنده تعالى، وكانت عادته اختيار ما أحبه الله داوم عليه.
[1] His statement: 'If it was ... etc.'; The gist of the answer: What the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) consistently practiced is of two types: One: Sunnah al-Huda, also called the emphasized Sunnah, which the one who abandons it is blamed. It results from consistent practice in a worshipful manner. Second: The additional Sunnah, which he consistently practiced as a matter of habit. It is equivalent to recommendation (istihbab) in that one is rewarded for it and not blamed for abandoning it. Consistent practice of using the right side (tayammun) is of the second type, so it is not an emphasized Sunnah, but rather recommended. [2] His statement: 'If it was'; i.e. the aforementioned consistency; in it: that it implies that occasional abandonment is considered in the additional Sunan, which would require excluding tayammun from them, since its abandonment is not established as mentioned. The verified view is that abandonment is not essential neither for Sunnah al-Huda nor for additional Sunan; the difference between them is only by worshipfulness and habit. (3) His statement: 'And this is understood'; The way of understanding is that his reasoning with the mentioned hadith indicates that tayammun was his habit in everything, even putting on sandals and combing hair. So mentioned by Mulla Isam. But there is criticism: the mentioned hadith does not indicate what he said. The more appropriate view is to say: The expression 'Allah loves' indicates that even if he was not commanded by Allah to use the right as an act of worship, rather because tayammun is beloved to Allah, and his habit was to choose what Allah loves, he consistently practiced it.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the classification of the Prophet's consistent practices (mawazibah) into two categories: Sunnan al-Huda (guidance sunnahs) and Sunnan al-Zawa'id (additional sunnahs). The author explains that the key distinction is not mere frequency or occasional abandonment, but the underlying intention: if the practice is done as an act of worship, it falls under Sunnan al-Huda (also called emphasized sunnah), whose abandonment is blameworthy. If it is done as a matter of habit, it falls under Sunnan al-Zawa'id, which is equivalent to recommended (mustahabb). The specific case of using the right side first (tayammun) is argued to be habitual, based on the hadith 'Allah loves tayammun in everything.' Thus, tayammun is mustahabb, not emphasized sunnah. The commentary also addresses an objection that Zawa'id require occasional abandonment; the author clarifies that abandonment is not a defining feature.

Key Terms
سنة الهدى (sunnah al-huda): The emphasized sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed as worship; abandoning it is blameworthy.
سنة الزوائد (sunnah al-zawa'id): Additional sunnahs that the Prophet did as habitual acts; rewarded for doing, not blamed for leaving.
التيامن (al-tayammun): Using the right side first in all actions, such as wearing shoes, entering, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary factor that distinguishes Sunnan al-Huda from Sunnan al-Zawa'id?
A) The frequency of the action
B) The occasional abandonment of the action
C) Whether the action is done intentionally as worship or habit
D) Whether the action is mentioned in the Quran

Key Takeaway
The distinction between Sunnah al-Huda and Sunnah al-Zawa'id rests on the Prophet's intention—worship yields emphasized sunnah, habit yields recommended sunnah.

Wiping the Neck in Wudu: Ruling and Evidence
Ruling on wiping the neck with evidence, including hadith scrutiny and Hanafi legal analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping the neck (mustahabb) and explain its evidence from the Prophet's action.

Core Idea
Wiping the neck is recommended (mustahabb) in wudu; the Prophet's action shows recommendation, not obligation.

This passage from Sharh al-Wiqayah clarifies the ruling on wiping the neck during wudu. The commentator examines the hadith evidence and establishes that the act is mustahabb (recommended), following the majority Hanafi position. We will trace the proof and note an intra-madhhab difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping the neck (masah al-raqabah). The ruling in the Hanafi school is mustahabb (recommended).
Mustahabb means recommended; omitting it does not affect validity.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's action (fi‘l) of wiping his neck, reported by Abu Dawud, al-Bazzar, al-Tahawi.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain) but accepted.
3
Analyze the dalalah
In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action (fi‘l) indicates istihbab (recommendation) unless there is evidence of obligation. Here, there is no command to wipe the neck, and the act is not done consistently as an emphasized worship.
Fi‘l al-nabi yields istihbab; qawl (command) yields wujub.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some later Hanafi scholars (e.g., Sharanbalali) considered it sunnah, but the mufta bihi is mustahabb.
The difference is one of degree; both agree it is recommended.
5
Conclusion: the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is mustahabb (recommended), based on the Prophet's action and the lack of evidence for obligation.

ومسح الرقبة) ؛ لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مسح عليها". [١] قوله : بقوله ... الخ ؛ هذا الحديث بهذا اللفظ لم يوجد في كتب الحديث كما صرح به العَيْني والزيلعي وابن حَجَر وغيرهم ، نعم ورد عن عائشة رضي الله عنها : «كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يحب التيامن في كلّ شيء في تنعله وترجله وشأنه كله، أخرجه التِّرْمِذِيِّ والنَّسَائيّ وغيرها، كما بسطناه في «غاية المقال فيما يتعلق بالنعال) وتعليقاته المسماة بـ«ظفر الأنفال». And (wiping the neck) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) wiped it. [1] His statement: 'By his statement...' etc.; This hadith with this wording is not found in hadith books as stated by al-‘Ayni, al-Zayla‘i, Ibn Hajar and others. Yes, it is narrated from ‘Aishah (may Allah be pleased with her): 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) loved tayammun in everything, in putting on sandals, combing hair, and all his affairs,' recorded by Tirmidhi and Nasa’i and others, as we elaborated in 'Ghayat al-Maqal' and its commentaries. [2] His statement: 'he wiped on them' is reported by Abu Dawud, al-Bazzar, al-Tahawi and others, and we have expanded the discussion on this topic in my treatise: 'Tuhfat al-Talabah fi Masah al-Raqabah' and its commentaries.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on wiping the neck (masah al-raqabah) during wudu. The base text (Sharh al-Wiqayah) mentions it, and the commentator clarifies the evidence. Two points are made: First, the hadith often cited for the neck wiping (the one mentioning tayammun) is not found in standard hadith works in that wording; but a similar hadith from ‘Aishah is authentic. Second, there is a specific hadith that the Prophet wiped his neck, reported by Abu Dawud and others. Based on these, the Hanafi school holds wiping the neck as recommended (mustahabb). Some later Hanafi scholars like Sharanbalali and Kashghari considered it sunnah, but the relied-upon position is mustahabb.

Key Terms
مسح الرقبة (masah al-raqabah): The act of wiping the back of the neck with wet hands during wudu.

Key Takeaway
Wiping the neck during wudu is mustahabb (recommended) based on the Prophet's action; it is not obligatory and does not affect the validity of wudu if omitted.

The Ruling on Wiping the Neck in Wudu
Explanation of the ruling on wiping the neck with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping the neck (masḥ al-raqabah) and explain the hadith evidence behind it.

Core Idea
Wiping the neck is mustahab (recommended) in wudu, supported by weak hadith but accepted for extra reward.

The Hanafi school includes wiping the neck (masḥ al-raqabah) as a recommended act in wudu. This lesson examines the passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah which discusses the evidence for this practice. We will explore the hadith cited, assess its strength, and understand why the Hanafis consider this act mustahab despite weak transmission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the specific act being discussed—wiping the neck (masḥ al-raqabah)—and the ruling assigned to it in the Hanafi school.
2
Find the primary proof (dalil)
Identify the hadith cited by the commentator: the narration that the Prophet (peace be upon him) wiped his neck. Note the source (Abu Dawud, al-Bazzar, al-Tahawi).
3
Assess the hadith's strength
Determine the reliability of the hadith. The commentator notes it is weak (zanni al-thubut) but supported by multiple chains.
thubut: zanni; dalala: zanni
4
Apply Hanafi usul to derive the hukm
Explain why a weak hadith leads to mustahab, not wajib. The Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates recommendation (istihbab) unless there is evidence of obligation.
Hanafi principle: Fi'l al-nabi yufid al-istihbab
5
Note intra-Hanafi variations
Some later Hanafi scholars (e.g., al-Shurunbulali) consider it sunnah, but the majority holds it as mustahab.

Nullification by Unusual Exits: Worms and Wind
Intra-Hanafi dispute on nullification by worm and wind

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on wudu nullification by unusual exits (worms and wind) from the two passages, distinguish the positions of Imam Muhammad and the majority, and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
An unusual exit nullifies wudu only if from the two passages; from the front, the ruling depends on the view regarding wind.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah expands the general rule that anything exiting the two passages nullifies wudu, but then delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute over unusual substances. When a worm or wind exits from the front or penis, scholars differ. We will dissect the arguments and settle on the relied-upon fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
The base text says that anything exiting the two passages (front and back) nullifies wudu, whether usual or unusual. Understand this as the starting point.
2
Analyze the worm cases
For a worm from the anus: consensus on nullification. For a worm from a woman's front: those who hold that wind from the front nullifies also hold that the worm nullifies; those who do not, disagree. The same applies to a worm from the penis.
The connecting factor is the view on wind.
3
Analyze the wind cases
Consensus that wind from the anus nullifies. Dispute on wind from the front or penis. Imam Muhammad (cited by al-Quduri) uses the general hadith to argue nullification. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf) restrict the hadith, holding it does not nullify unless accompanied by a condition (e.g., foul smell or abnormal passage).
The core dalil is the hadith 'Wudu is only nullified by what exits from the front or back' (al-Daraqutni).
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a woman who passes wind from her front must renew wudu according to Imam Muhammad, but not according to the majority. This affects daily practice for many women.
The dispute has real-life impact.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The commentator leans toward the majority position: wind from the front does not nullify. This is the relied-upon fatwa in the later Hanafi school, as recorded in al-Wiqayah and others.
The mufta bihi provides clarity for practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وناقضه : ما خرج من السبيلين سواء كان معتاداً ، أو غير معتاد : كالدودة والريح [١] قوله : كالدودة ؛ فإن خروجها غير معتاد : فإن خرجت من الدبرِ نقض الوضوء اتفاقاً. وإن كانت خارجة من قبل المرأة اختلفوا فيه، فالذين قالوا بنقض الريح الخارجة من القبل قالوا : بنقضها أيضاً، ومن لم يقل به لم يقل به. وإن خرجت من الذكر اختلفوا فيه أيضاً ، فذكر الشارح له فيما سيأتي أنها غير ناقضة، وذكر في «الخلاصة»، و«فتاوی قاضي خان» : إنها ناقضة. هذا كله إذا كانت خارجة من أحد السبيلين، فإن خرجت من غيرهما لا تنقض، سواء خرجت من الفم أو الأنف أو الجراحة. كذا في «الذخيرة». [٢] قوله : والريح ؛ اتفق أصحابنا وغيرهم على نقض الريح الخارجة من الدبر. واختلفوا في الخارجة من القبل والذكر : فذكر القدوري عن محمد أنها توجب الوضوء، ودليله: عموم حديث : لا ينقض الوضوء إلا ما خرج من قبل أو دبر، أخرجه الدارقطني في كتاب «غرائب مالك».
And its nullifier: what exits from the two passages, whether usual or unusual, such as a worm and wind. [1] His saying: 'such as a worm'; because its exit is unusual. If it exits from the anus, it nullifies wudu by consensus. If it exits from a woman’s front, there is disagreement: those who say that wind exiting from the front nullifies also say it nullifies; those who do not say that, do not say it nullifies. If it exits from the penis, there is also disagreement. The commentator mentions later that it does not nullify, but it is mentioned in al-Khulasah and Fatawa Qadi Khan that it does nullify. All of this is if it exits from one of the two passages. If it exits from elsewhere, it does not nullify, whether from the mouth, nose, or a wound. This is in al-Dhakhirah. [2] His saying: 'and wind'; our companions and others agree that wind exiting from the anus nullifies wudu. They differ regarding wind exiting from the front and the penis. Al-Quduri narrated from Muhammad that it necessitates wudu, and his evidence is the general hadith: 'Wudu is only nullified by what exits from the front or the back' recorded by al-Daraqutni in the book Ghara’ib Malik.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage deals with what nullifies wudu (nawaqid). The main text states that anything exiting the two passages (front and back) nullifies wudu, whether it is usual (like urine and stool) or unusual (like a worm or wind). The commentator then explains each case. For a worm: if it exits from the anus, all scholars agree it nullifies wudu. If from a woman’s front, there is a difference among Hanafi scholars: those who consider wind from the front as nullifying also consider worm from the front as nullifying; otherwise not. If from the penis, there is also disagreement: some say it nullifies, others not. The commentator notes that if the worm exits from anywhere other than the two passages (e.g., mouth, nose, wound), it does not nullify wudu. For wind (passing gas): there is consensus that wind from the anus nullifies wudu. However, for wind exiting from the front or penis, there is a difference. According to Imam Muhammad (as narrated by al-Quduri), it does nullify, citing the general hadith 'Wudu is only nullified by what exits from the front or back.' This indicates that any exit from these areas nullifies. Other Hanafi scholars may take a stricter view. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that wind from the front of a woman does not nullify wudu unless it is accompanied by a foul smell or the woman is 'mufda' (having an abnormal passage). This is a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute.

Key Terms
ناقض (naqid): That which nullifies wudu.
السبيلين (al-sabilayn): The two passages: front (urinary/reproductive) and back (anus).
الدودة (al-dudah): Worm; an unusual exit that may nullify wudu if from the passages.
الريح (al-reeh): Wind/gas exiting from the body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, does a worm exiting from a woman’s front nullify wudu?
A) Yes, by consensus
B) No, because it is not a usual exit
C) It depends: if wind from front nullifies, then yes; otherwise no
D) Only if it exits from the back

Key Takeaway
An unusual exit nullifies wudu only if from the two passages; the intra-Hanafi dispute on wind from the front is resolved by adopting the majority view that it does not nullify unless there is an abnormal condition.

Wind from Front Passage: Does It Nullify Wudu?
Intra-Hanafi dispute with tarjih on front wind nullification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on wind from the front passage nullifying wudu and identify the exceptional case of the mufdat woman.

Core Idea
Wind from the front does not nullify wudu — unless it likely came from the back.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether wind exiting from a woman's front or male urethra nullifies wudu. The majority holds it does not, based on two arguments: it is usually a muscular tremor (ikhtilaj) rather than actual wind, or if it is wind, it has not passed over impurity. A special case arises when a woman's vaginal and rectal passages have merged (mufdat), where caution is recommended because the wind may have come from the back.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
The act in question is the emission of wind (or sensation) from the front passage (of a woman or from the male urethra). The disputed ruling is whether this nullifies wudu (naqid) or not.
Standard nullifiers include wind from the back, but front emission is contested.
2
Understand the two reasons for the majority position
The authors of Al-Hidayah, Al-Munyah, and Al-Muhit give two arguments: (1) it is not actual wind but a tremor (ikhtilaj), and (2) even if it is wind, it has not passed over any impurity (unlike wind from the back which passes over feces).
The second argument relies on the principle that an emission is only impure if it passes over impurity.
3
Recognize the exceptional case of the mufdat woman
A woman whose vaginal and rectal passages have merged (mufdat) is a special case. Since the two openings are connected, wind from the front might originate from the back. Therefore, it is recommended (mustahabb) for her to perform wudu if she experiences such wind, and some scholars even say it is obligatory.
This exception shows the importance of the underlying cause: impurity transfer.
4
Note the difference of opinion (qil) and the tarjih
Some Hanafi scholars (qil) held that wind from the front always nullifies wudu. However, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it does not, as declared by the majority. The minority view is considered weak.
This illustrates how tarjih works within the Hanafi school even when the source (qil) is anonymous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخارجة من القبل والذكر، وفيه اختلاف المشايخ. وصحَّحَ صاحب «الهداية» و «المنية» و«المحيط» وغيرهم : عدم نقضها قائلين : إنها اختلاج لا ريح، وإن كانت ريحاً فلا نجاسة، وريح الدبر ناقضة لمرورها بالنجاسة، ولو كانت المرأة مفضاةً أتحد سبيلاها، يستحب لها الوضوء بالريح الخارجة من القبل؛ لاحتمال كونها من الدبر. ذكره في «السراجية»، وقيل : يجب عليها الوضوء.
Exiting from the front and the male organ, and concerning it there is disagreement of the mashayikh. And the author of Al-Hidayah, Al-Munyah, Al-Muhit and others declared its not nullifying, saying: it is a tremor not wind, and if it is wind then there is no impurity, and wind from the anus is nullifying because it passes over impurity. And if a woman is mufdat (her two passages have become one), it is recommended for her to perform wudu due to the wind exiting from the front, because it may be from the anus. Mentioned in Al-Sirajiyyah. And it was said: wudu becomes obligatory upon her.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage addresses a disputed issue within the Hanafi school: whether wind (ريح) exiting from the front passage (قبل) of a woman or from the male urethra (ذكر) nullifies wudu. The relied-upon position, as declared by the authors of Al-Hidayah, Al-Munyah, Al-Muhit, and others, is that it does NOT nullify wudu. They give two reasons: first, such emission is usually a muscular tremor or movement (اختلاج) rather than actual wind; second, even if it were wind, it has not passed over impurity (unlike wind from the back which passes over feces), so it remains pure. Therefore, it does not break wudu. There is an exceptional case of a woman whose vaginal and rectal passages have merged (مفضاة) due to a fistula. In such a case, wind from the front is suspected to have originated from the back (because the openings are connected), so it is recommended (يستحب) – not obligatory – for her to perform wudu for that wind. However, some scholars (قيل) held that it becomes obligatory. The passage concludes by noting the difference of opinion.

Key Terms
اختلاج (ikhtilāj): A muscular tremor or spasm, not actual wind.
مفضاة (mufḍāh): A woman whose vaginal and rectal passages have merged into one opening, often due to a fistula.
ناقض (nāqiḍ): That which breaks or nullifies wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on wind exiting from a woman's front passage?
A) It always nullifies wudu.
B) It does not nullify wudu because it is considered a tremor or clean air.
C) It nullifies wudu only if the woman is mufdat.
D) It is obligatory to perform wudu due to it.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, only wind from the back nullifies wudu; wind from the front does not, except in the case of a mufdat woman where caution is recommended.

Resolving Pronoun Reference: Wind, Worms, and the Scope of Disagreement in Nullifiers
Super-commentator refutes a previous analysis of the pronoun in 'fīhi'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the reasoning behind the pronoun reference debate and identify the correct scope of disagreement among Hanafi scholars regarding nullification of unusual emissions.

Core Idea
The pronoun 'fīhi' can refer to 'ghayr mu‘tād', not just wind—proving disagreement applies only to certain unusual nullifiers, not all.

This lesson delves into a subtle yet critical textual analysis from 'Umdat al-Ri‘āyah, where the super-commentator (the author) systematically refutes the earlier claim of Akhi Chalabi concerning the pronoun in 'wa fīhi ikhtilāf al-mashāyikh'. The debate is not mere grammar; it determines the scope of a legal disagreement on what nullifies wudu. Understanding this analysis sharpens your ability to read Hanafi fiqh texts with precision and to appreciate how scholars argue over the implications of a single word.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested pronoun
Locate the pronoun 'fīhi' in the phrase 'wa fīhi ikhtilāf al-mashāyikh'. The debate is over its antecedent: does it refer to 'wind' (al-rīh) or to 'ghayr mu‘tād' (unusual emission)?
The antecedent determines whether the disagreement is only on wind (as Akhi Chalabi claimed) or on certain unusual emissions (as the super-commentator argues).
2
Examine Akhi Chalabi's argument
Akhi Chalabi argued that the pronoun must refer to wind because if it referred to 'ghayr mu‘tād', it would include the worm (dūdah), which is unanimously a nullifier—contradicting the word 'ikhtilāf' (disagreement). Understand his reasoning: he considered the worm from the anus as the only type and believed there is no disagreement on worms.
He also claimed that the commentator would later negate disagreement on the worm from the urethra.
3
Analyze the super-commentator's first objection
The super-commentator counters that the pronoun can indeed refer to 'ghayr mu‘tād', and the disagreement is only about some individuals of 'ghayr mu‘tād' (e.g., worm from front and male organ), not all. The unanimous nullification of the anal worm does not negate disagreement on others.
This shows the importance of specifying which types of unusual emissions are disputed.
4
Follow the remaining five objections
Step through objections 2–6: (2) The worm in the commentary is general, not specific to anus; (3) Repetition is acceptable; (4) The repetition is inevitable anyway; (5) The entailment (that worm of urethra is disputed) is accepted; (6) The commentator's future statement does not negate the disagreement on worm of urethra.
Each objection strengthens the case for a broader reading.
5
Conclude on the scope of ikhtilāf
Synthesize: The correct view is that the disagreement (ikhtilāf) among the mashāyikh includes not only wind from unusual passages but also certain unusual emissions like worms from the front and male organ. This understanding aligns with the super-commentator's analysis.
The practical implication: when issuing fatwa, one must recognize that nullification of these unusual emissions is not settled by consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١] قوله : وفيه ; قال أخي جلبي في «ذخيرة العقبى»: «الصحيح أن يرجع ضمير فيه إلى الريح باعتبار المذكور؛ لأنّ فيها خلافاً سواء خرجت من قبل المرأة أو إحليل الرجل، ولا يجوز أن يرجع إلى لفظ الغير في قوله : «غير معتاد» ؛ لأن الدودة داخلة فيه، ولا اختلاف في كونها ناقضةً ; لأنّ المراد هاهنا دودة الدبر ; لأن الكلام فيما خرج من السبيلين. وسيجيء التصريح من الشارح باختلاف المشايخ في دودة قبل المرأة، فالظاهر أن يحمل هذا الاختلاف على الريح ; لئلا يلزم التكرار، وأيضاً يلزم أن تكون دودة الإحليل مختلفاً فيها، وسيصرِّحُ الشارحُ بنفي ذلك بقوله : ومن الاحليل لا. انتهى

أقول : فيه مؤاخذات :
الأولى : في قوله : «لا يجوز» .... الخ ; فإنّه يجوز أن يرجع الضمير إلى الغير، ويكون المقصود من الاختلافِ الاختلافُ في غيرِ المعتاد بحسب بعض أفراده لا في نقض غير المعتاد من حيث هو غير معتاد، ويكون المعنى أن في نقض غير المعتاد اختلافاً، فإنّهم اتفقوا على نقض المعتاد، وأن كل معتاد ناقض.
واختلفوا في نقض غير المعتاد، فمنه ما هو ناقض اتفاقاً ; كدودة الدبر، ومنه ما هو ناقض عند بعضهم دون بعضهم كدودة القُبل والذكر وريحهما ، وما في «البحر» عن «السراج الوهاج»، و«الدر المختار» عن «الجوهرة النيرة»: إن نقض دودة القُبل إجماعي، ليس بصحيح. ويجوز أيضاً أن يرجع إلى كل من الدودة والريحين، أما الخلاف في الريحين فواضح ، وأما في الدودة فباعتبار بعض أفرادها، وهو دودةُ القُبل والذكر. الثانية : في تخصيصه الدودة المذكورة في الشرح بالخارجة من الدبر، فإن الظاهر أن المراد أعم منها ومن دودة القُبل والذكر، بل لو جعل لفظ الخارجة صفة لكل من الدودة والريح لم يبعد. الثالثة : في قوله : لئلا يلزم التكرار»، فإنّ مثل هذا التكرار بأن يكون الحكم مذكوراً في موضع صراحةً وفي موضع ضمناً، ليس مستنكر. الرابعة : إن التكرار الذي فرّ عنه لازم على ما اختاره أيضاً من حمل الدودة على دودة الدبر أيضاً ; فإنّه سيصرّح الشارحُ بحكمها بقوله : «وأما الخارجة من الدبر فتنقض» ... الخ.
الخامسة : في قوله : «وأيضاً يلزم»... الخ، فإنّ اللازم يلتزم كما عرفته. السادسة : في قوله : «وسيصرح الشارح»... الخ، حوالة غير صحيحة، فإنّ
عبارة الشارح فيما سيأتي لا يدل على نفي الاختلاف فيه.
His statement: 'and concerning it' – Akhi Chalabi said in 'Dhakirat al-'Uqba: 'The correct view is that the pronoun in 'fīhi' refers to wind by considering what is mentioned, because concerning it there is disagreement whether it exits from a woman's front or a man's urethra, and it is not permissible to refer it to the word 'ghayr' in his statement 'ghayr mu'tād', because the worm is included in it, and there is no disagreement on its being a nullifier; for the intended here is the worm of the anus, because the discussion is about what exits from the two passages. And the clear statement will come from the commentator about the disagreement of the mashayikh on the worm of the woman's front, so it is apparent that this disagreement is carried on the wind, to avoid repetition, and also it would entail that the worm of the urethra is disputed, and the commentator will explicitly negate that by his statement 'From the urethra, no.' End.

I say: There are objections in it:
First: In his statement 'it is not permissible' etc. – because it is permissible that the pronoun refer to 'ghayr', and the intended meaning of the disagreement is the disagreement regarding the 'ghayr mu'tād' with respect to some of its individuals, not the nullification of the 'ghayr mu'tād' as such. So the meaning is that in the nullification of the 'ghayr mu'tād' there is disagreement, for they agreed on the nullification of the mu'tād, and every mu'tād is a nullifier. And they disagreed on the nullification of the 'ghayr mu'tād', among which is a definite nullifier by consensus, such as the worm of the anus, and among it is a nullifier according to some but not others, such as the worm of the front and the male organ and their wind. And what is in 'al-Bahr' from 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj' and 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar' from 'al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah' that the nullification of the worm of the front is unanimous is not correct. And it is also permissible that it refer to both the worm and the two winds. As for the disagreement on the two winds, it is clear. And as for the worm, it is by considering some of its individuals, namely the worm of the front and the male organ. Second: In his specification of the worm mentioned in the commentary as exiting from the anus, whereas the apparent is that the intended is more general, including it and the worm of the front and the male organ. Rather, if one makes the word 'al-khārijah' an attribute of both the worm and the wind, it would not be far. Third: In his statement 'to avoid repetition' – such repetition, where the ruling is mentioned explicitly in one place and implicitly in another, is not objectionable. Fourth: The repetition he fled from is necessary according to his own choice of carrying the worm as the worm of the anus, for the commentator will later state its ruling by saying: 'As for that exiting from the anus, it nullifies' etc. Fifth: In his statement 'and also it would entail' – he accepts the entailment as I have explained. Sixth: In his statement 'the commentator will explicitly negate that' – this reference is invalid, for the commentator's forthcoming phrase does not indicate a negation of disagreement in it.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a hashiya-style critical analysis by the author of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah. He reviews the comment of Akhi Chalabi in 'Dhakirat al-'Uqba', who argued that the pronoun in 'fīhi' (in the phrase 'wa fīhi ikhtilāf al-mashāyikh') must refer to 'wind' (al-rīh) and cannot refer to 'ghayr mu'tād' (unusual) because that would include the worm (dūdah) which is unanimously a nullifier. The present author rejects each of Akhi Chalabi's six points systematically. 

First: He shows that the pronoun can refer to 'ghayr mu'tād', and the disagreement is about some individuals of 'ghayr mu'tād' not all. Second: He argues that the worm in the commentary could be general, including those from front and back. Third: He dismisses the claim of avoiding repetition as acceptable. Fourth: He notes that the repetition is necessary anyway. Fifth: He accepts the entailment. Sixth: He shows that the commentator's future statement does not negate disagreement. 

This is a detailed example of Hanafi textual analysis (taḥqīq al-‘ibārah) where the precise scope of a difference of opinion is clarified through grammatical and contextual reasoning. The author aims to defend a broader reading that allows for multiple interpretations of the pronoun, contra Akhi Chalabi's restrictive view.

Key Terms
ضمير (ḍamīr): A pronoun; specifically, the pronoun in 'fīhi' whose antecedent is debated.
غير معتاد (ghayr mu‘tād): That which is unusual or not normal; in context, emissions that are not typical (e.g., worms, rare winds).
دودة (dūdah): A worm; specifically, worms exiting from the passages, which may be from the anus or front.

Key Takeaway
Pronoun reference in fiqh texts can determine the scope of legal disagreement; careful grammatical analysis is essential to correctly identify which rulings are contested and which are settled.

Meaning of 'or from Other' in Nullifiers of Wudu
Grammatical clarification of 'aw min ghayrihi' in wudu nullifiers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the grammatical resolution of the phrase 'aw min ghayrihi' and state that the nullifier applies to excretion from each passage individually.

Core Idea
The pronoun in 'ghayrihi' refers to each passage individually, not both together.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies a grammatical ambiguity in the matn of al-Hidayah regarding the nullifiers of wudu. The author, Imam al-Mahbubi, resolves the pronoun reference in 'aw min ghayrihi' by interpreting the dual 'al-sabilayn' distributively—meaning each one of the two passages individually. This grammatical point has a direct legal implication: any excretion from either passage nullifies wudu, not only when both exit simultaneously.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical issue
The pronoun 'hi' in 'ghayrihi' requires an antecedent. In the phrase 'ahad al-sabilayn' (one of the two passages), 'ahad' is singular, so 'ghayrihi' conjoins smoothly. Without 'ahad', 'ghayrihi' appears to refer to the dual 'al-sabilayn', which is grammatically inconsistent.
2
Examine the two manuscript traditions
Some manuscripts include 'ahad' (one), making the grammar straightforward. Others omit 'ahad', creating the pronoun reference problem.
3
Understand the author's resolution
The author rejects weak proposed solutions (tawjīhāt bāridah) and gives the correct interpretation: 'ma kharaja min al-sabilayn' means 'what exits from each one of the two passages individually'. The dual is read distributively, so the singular pronoun refers to each one.
This distributive reading (tawzi') solves the grammatical issue.
4
Apply the legal implication
The ruling is that any impurity exiting from either the front or back passage individually nullifies wudu, not only when both exit together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١] قوله : أو من غيره : أي الخارج من غير السبيلين، فهو معطوف على قوله : «أحد السبيلين»، وضميره راجع إلى الأحد، هذا على ما في بعض النسخ ، وأما على ما في بعضها من ترك لفظ الأحدِ فارجاعُ ضمير غيره إلى التثنية مشكل.
وقد اختار الناظرون لدفعه توجيهات باردة ذكرنا بطلانها في «السعاية»(۳) ، والأوجه أن يقال : معنى ما خرج من السبيلين، ما خرج من كل واحد من السبيلين ; لظهور أنّ الناقض ليس ما خرج من السبيلين معا، بل ما خرج من كل واحدٍ واحد على حدة، فحينئذ فلا إشكال في إرجاع الضمير.
His statement: 'or from other' means: what exits from other than the two passages, so it is conjoined to his statement 'one of the two passages', and its pronoun refers to 'one', this is according to some copies. But according to others, which omitted the word 'one', the reference of the pronoun of 'other' to the dual is problematic. And the researchers have chosen for resolving it cold explanations, which we have mentioned their invalidity in Al-Si'ayah. The appropriate view is to say: the meaning of 'what exited from the two passages' is 'what exited from each one of the two passages', because it is evident that the nullifier is not what exited from both passages together, but what exited from each one individually, so then there is no problem in referring the pronoun.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage resolves a grammatical ambiguity in the original text (matn) regarding the phrase 'أو من غيره' (or from other). The matn says: 'ma kharaja min ahad al-sabilayn aw min ghayrihi' – what exits from one of the two passages or from other. The word 'ghayrihi' (other) has a pronoun 'hi' that needs an antecedent. The author explains that in some manuscripts, 'ghayrihi' is conjoined to 'ahad' (one), so the pronoun refers to 'ahad'. In other manuscripts where 'ahad' is omitted, it becomes problematic because 'ghayrihi' (masculine singular) would need to refer to the dual 'al-sabilayn' (the two passages), which is grammatically inconsistent. The author dismisses weak attempts (tawjīhāt bāridah) to fix this and gives the correct interpretation: The phrase 'ma kharaja min al-sabilayn' actually means 'what exits from each one of the two passages individually', not both together. Therefore, the pronoun can refer to that implied singular concept (each one). This clarifies that 'or from other' means the same ruling applies to anything exiting from either passage singly.

Key Terms
غيره (ghayrihi): Other than it; the word 'other' with a pronoun, meaning 'other than the two passages'.
معطوف (ma‘ṭūf): Conjoined; a grammatical term indicating that 'ghayrihi' is connected to the previous word.
تثنية (tathniyah): Dual form; here, the word 'al-sabilayn' is dual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It means what exits from each of the two passages individually.

D) It means what exits from the anus only.

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'aw min ghayrihi' in the nullifiers of wudu is correctly understood as referring to excretion from each of the two passages individually, resolving a grammatical ambiguity.
